<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;"><a href="/wiki/File:French_empire.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/French_empire.svg/390px-French_empire.svg.png" decoding="async" width="390" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/French_empire.svg/585px-French_empire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/French_empire.svg/780px-French_empire.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:French_empire.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the first (green) and second (blue — plain and hatched) French colonial empires</div></div></div>
<p>During the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French colonization of the Americas</a> began with the creation of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>. It was followed by <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a>'s trading posts in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> in the 17th century. France had its "First colonial empire" from 1534 until 1814, including <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a>), <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>), <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">Gorée</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritius Island">Mauritius Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a>) and <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French India</a>.
</p><p>Its "Second colonial empire" began with the conquest of <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> in 1830 and came for the most part to an end with the granting of independence to <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The French imperial history was marked by numerous wars, large and small, and also by significant help to France itself from the colonials in the world wars.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> France took control of Algeria in 1830 but began in earnest to rebuild its worldwide empire after 1850, concentrating chiefly in North and West Africa (<a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a>), as well as South-East Asia (<a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>), with other conquests in the South Pacific (<a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>). France also twice attempted to make Mexico a colony in 1838–39 and in 1861-67 (see <a href="/wiki/Pastry_War" title="Pastry War">Pastry War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_French_intervention_in_Mexico" title="Second French intervention in Mexico">Second French intervention in Mexico</a>).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/170px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/255px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/340px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="934" data-file-height="1370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French poster about the "<a href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_Wars" title="Franco-Hova Wars">Madagascar War</a>"</div></div></div>
<p>French Republicans, at first hostile to empire, only became supportive when Germany started to build her own colonial empire. As it developed, the new empire took on roles of trade with France, supplying raw materials and purchasing manufactured items, as well as lending prestige to the motherland and spreading French civilization and language as well as Catholicism. It also provided crucial manpower in both World Wars.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> It became a moral justification to lift the world up to French standards by bringing Christianity and French culture. In 1884 the leading exponent of colonialism, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Ferry" title="Jules Ferry">Jules Ferry</a> declared France had a <a href="/wiki/Civilising_mission" class="mw-redirect" title="Civilising mission">civilising mission</a>: "The higher races have a right over the lower races, they have a duty to civilize the inferior".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>  Full citizenship rights – <i>assimilation</i> – were offered, although in reality assimilation was always on the distant horizon.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Contrasting from Britain, France sent small numbers of settlers to its colonies, with the only notable exception of Algeria, where French settlers nevertheless always remained a small minority.
</p><p>In the 19th and 20th centuries, the French colonial empire was the second-largest colonial empire in the world behind the British Empire, extending over 12,347,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,767,000 sq. miles) at its height in the 1920s and 1930s. France controlled nearly 1/10th of the Earth's land area, with a population of 110&#160;million people on the eve of World War II (5% of the world's population at the time).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In World War II, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free French</a> used the overseas colonies as bases from which they fought to liberate France. However, after 1945 anti-colonial movements began to challenge the Empire. France fought and lost a bitter war in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> in the 1950s. Whereas they won the war in Algeria, de Gaulle decided to grant Algeria independence anyway in 1962. French settlers and many local supporters relocated to France. Nearly all of France's colonies gained independence by 1960, but France retained great financial and diplomatic influence. It has repeatedly sent troops to assist its former colonies in Africa in suppressing insurrections and coups d'état.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ostende_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ostende Company (page does not exist)">Ostende Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_former_German_colonies" title="List of former German colonies">List of former German colonies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German colonial empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_colonial.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/German_colonial.PNG/280px-German_colonial.PNG" decoding="async" width="280" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/German_colonial.PNG/420px-German_colonial.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/German_colonial.PNG/560px-German_colonial.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_colonial.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German colonial empire, the third largest <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">colonial empire</a> during the 19th century after the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Second_French_colonial_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Second French colonial empire">French</a> ones<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>German expansion into Slavic lands begins in 12th-13th-century (see <a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">Drang nach Osten</a>). The concept of Drang nach Osten was a core element of German nationalism and a major element of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_ideology" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi ideology">Nazi ideology</a>. However the German involvement in the seizure of overseas territories was negligible until the end of the 19th century. Prussia unified the other states into the <a href="/wiki/Second_German_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Second German Empire">second German Empire</a> in 1871. Its Chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> (1862–90), long opposed colonial acquisitions, arguing that the burden of obtaining, maintaining, and defending such possessions would outweigh any potential benefits. He felt that colonies did not pay for themselves, that the German bureaucratic system would not work well in the tropics and the diplomatic disputes over colonies would distract Germany from its central interest, Europe itself.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, public opinion and elite opinion in Germany demanded colonies for reasons of international prestige, so Bismarck was forced to oblige. In 1883–84 Germany began to build a colonial empire in Africa and the South Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>  The establishment of the <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German colonial empire</a> started with <a href="/wiki/German_New_Guinea" title="German New Guinea">German New Guinea</a> in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>German colonies included the present territories of in Africa: <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a>; in Oceania: <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Solomon islands">Solomon islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>; and in Asia: <a href="/wiki/Tsingtao" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsingtao">Tsingtao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chefoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Chefoo">Chefoo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jiaozhou_Bay" title="Jiaozhou Bay">Jiaozhou Bay</a>. Also all German colonies were lost after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and given either to Britain (modern-day Tanzania, Namibia, parts of Cameroon and Pacific Ocean islands), France (most of Cameroon, Togo) and Belgium (Burundi and Rwanda). Italy, the 4th and last European power on the continent, received very little despite its significant involvement in the war alongside the Entente.
</p><p>By the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> Germany was deprived of part of the territories that became part of the formed independent Poland. However, most of the captured lands remained in Germany. Finally, Germany was deprived of the captured territories following the settlement of <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> in 1945, when new territories were annexed to Poland and the USSR. Moreover, in order to prevent a repetition of the historical events of German history, a cardinal decision was taken. As part of their wartime goals, the Western allies and USSR sought the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_Prussia" title="Abolition of Prussia">abolition of Prussia</a>. By Law No. 46, which was accepted and implemented by the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Control_Council" title="Allied Control Council">Allied Control Council</a> on 25 February 1947, Prussia, as "from early days has been a bearer of militarism and reaction in Germany", was officially proclaimed to be dissolved.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_territories_occupied_by_Imperial_Japan" title="List of territories occupied by Imperial Japan">List of territories occupied by Imperial Japan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Empire_(orthographic_projection).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/250px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/375px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/500px-Japanese_Empire_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Empire_(orthographic_projection).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere in 1942</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx,_June_11th.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg/220px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg/330px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg/440px-Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx%2C_June_11th.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1263" data-file-height="921" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japanese_Special_Naval_Landing_Forces_on_the_deck_board_of_the_IJN_xxx,_June_11th.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Special_Naval_Landing_Forces" title="Special Naval Landing Forces">Japanese Marines</a> preparing to land in <a href="/wiki/Anqing" title="Anqing">Anqing</a> China in June 1938.</div></div></div>
<p>For over 200 years, Japan maintained a feudal society during a period of <a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">relative isolation from the rest of the world</a>. However, in the 1850s, <a href="/wiki/Perry_Expedition" title="Perry Expedition">military pressure from the United States</a> and other world powers coerced Japan to open itself to the global market, resulting in an end to the country's isolation. A <a href="/wiki/Bakumatsu" title="Bakumatsu">period of conflicts and political revolutions</a> followed due to socioeconomic uncertainty, ending in 1868 with the reunification of political power under the <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">Japanese Emperor</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Meiji_Restoration" title="Meiji Restoration">Meiji Restoration</a>. This sparked a period of rapid <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> driven in part by a Japanese desire for self-sufficiency. By the early 1900s, Japan was a naval power that could hold its own against an established European power as it defeated Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite its rising population and increasingly industrialized economy, Japan had relatively little territory and lacked significant natural resources. As a result, the country turned to imperialism and <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a> in part as a means of compensating for these shortcomings, adopting the national motto <i>"<a href="/wiki/Fukoku_ky%C5%8Dhei" title="Fukoku kyōhei">Fukoku kyōhei</a>"</i> (富国強兵, "Enrich the state, strengthen the military").<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>And Japan was eager to take every opportunity. In 1869 they took advantage of the defeat of the rebels of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ezo" title="Republic of Ezo">Republic of Ezo</a> to incorporate definitely the island of <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a> to Japan. For centuries, Japan viewed the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a> as one of its provinces. In 1871 the <a href="/wiki/Mudan_incident" title="Mudan incident">Mudan incident</a> happened: <a href="/wiki/Paiwan_people" title="Paiwan people">cannibal Taiwanese aborigines</a> murdered 54 <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_people" title="Ryukyuan people">Ryūkyūan</a> sailors that had their ship shipwrecked. At that time the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a> were claimed by both <a href="/wiki/Qing_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing China">Qing China</a> and Japan, and the Japanese interpreted the incident as an attack on their citizens. They took steps to bring the islands in their jurisdiction: in 1872 the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Domain" title="Ryukyu Domain">Ryukyu Domain</a> was declared, and in 1874 a <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Taiwan_(1874)" title="Japanese invasion of Taiwan (1874)">retaliatory incursion to Taiwan</a> was sent, which was a success. The success of this expedition emboldened the Japanese: not even the Americans could defeat the Taiwanese cannibals in the <a href="/wiki/Formosa_Expedition" title="Formosa Expedition">Formosa Expedition</a> of 1867. Very few gave it much thought at the time, but this was the first move in the Japanese expansionism series. Japan occupied Taiwan for the rest of 1874 and then left owing to Chinese pressures, but in 1879 it finally annexed the <a href="/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands" title="Ryukyu Islands">Ryukyu Islands</a>. In 1875 Qing China sent a 300-men force to subdue the Taiwanese cannibals, but unlike the Japanese the Chinese were routed, ambushed and 250 of their men were killed; the failure of this expedition exposed once more the failure of Qing China to exert effective control in Taiwan, and acted as another incentive for the Japanese to annex Taiwan. Eventually, the spoils for winning the <a href="/wiki/First_Sino-Japanese_War" title="First Sino-Japanese War">First Sino-Japanese War</a> in 1894 included <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1875 Japan took its first operation against <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Joseon" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Joseon">Joseon Korea</a>, another territory that for centuries it coveted; the <a href="/wiki/Ganghwa_Island_incident" title="Ganghwa Island incident">Ganghwa Island incident</a> made Korea open to international trade. <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> was annexed in 1910. As a result of winning the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> in 1905, Japan took part of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin Island</a> from Russia. Precisely, the victory against the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> shook the world: never before an Asian nation defeated a European power, and in Japan it was seen as a feat. Japan's victory against Russia would act as an antecedent for Asian countries in the fight against the Western powers for <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">Decolonization</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Japan took German-leased territories in China's Shandong Province, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, and kept the islands as League of nations mandates. At first, Japan was in good standing with the victorious Allied powers of World War I, but different discrepancies and dissatisfaction with the rewards of the treaties cooled the relations with them, for example American pressure forced it to return the Shandong area. By the '30s, economic depression, urgency of resources and a growing distrust in the Allied powers made Japan lean to a hardened militaristic stance. Through the decade, it would grow closer to Germany and Italy, forming together the Axis alliance. In 1931 Japan took <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Manchuria</a> from China. International reactions condemned this move, but Japan's already strong skepticism against Allied nations meant that it nevertheless carried on.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg/220px-First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg/330px-First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg/440px-First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1247" data-file-height="863" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_pictures_of_the_Japanese_occupation_of_Peiping_in_China.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japanese march into <a href="/wiki/Zhengyangmen" title="Zhengyangmen">Zhengyangmen</a> of <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> after capturing the city in July 1937.</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> in 1937, Japan's military invaded central China. Also, in 1938-1939 Japan made an attempt to seize the territory of Soviet Russia and Mongolia, but suffered a serious defeats (see <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Khasan" title="Battle of Lake Khasan">Battle of Lake Khasan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol" title="Battles of Khalkhin Gol">Battles of Khalkhin Gol</a>). By now, relations with the Allied powers were at the bottom, and an international boycott against Japan to deprive it of natural resources was enforced. Thus a military move to gain access to them was needed, and so Japan <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attacked Pearl Harbor</a>, bringing the United States to World War II. Using its superior technological advances in <a href="/wiki/Naval_aviation" title="Naval aviation">naval aviation</a> and its modern doctrines of <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">naval warfare</a>, Japan achieved one of the fastest maritime expansions in history. By 1942 Japan had conquered much of East Asia and the Pacific, including the east of China, Hong Kong, Thailand, Vietnam, Cambodia, Burma (Myanmar), Malaysia,  the Philippines, Indonesia, part of <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> and many islands of the Pacific Ocean. Just as Japan's late industrialization success and victory against the Russian Empire was seen as an example among underdeveloped Asia-Pacific nations, the Japanese took advantage of this and promoted among its conquered the goal to jointly create an anti-European "<a href="/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Co-Prosperity_Sphere" title="Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere">Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere</a>". This plan helped the Japanese gain support from native populations during its conquests, especially in Indonesia. However, the United States had a vastly stronger military and industrial base and defeated Japan, stripping it of conquests and returning its settlers back to Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Empire">Ottoman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ottoman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg/220px-Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg/330px-Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg/440px-Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg 2x" data-file-width="830" data-file-height="624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aleppo-OttomantroopsTopicalpressagency.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ottoman troops marching in <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire">Territorial evolution of the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<p>The Ottoman Empire was an imperial state that lasted from 1299 to 1922. In 1453, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_the_Conqueror" title="Mehmed the Conqueror">Mehmed the Conqueror</a> besieged the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Fall of Constantinople</a> after 1,500 years of Roman rule, thereafter making it the capital of the empire. During the 16th and 17th centuries, in particular at the height of its power under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman the Magnificent</a>, the Ottoman Empire was a powerful multinational, multilingual empire, which invaded and colonized much of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>. Its repeated invasions, and brutal treatment of Slavs led to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migrations_of_the_Serbs" title="Great Migrations of the Serbs">Great Migrations of the Serbs</a> to escape persecution. At the beginning of the 17th century the empire contained <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Provinces of the Ottoman Empire">32 provinces</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/Vassal_and_tributary_states_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Vassal and tributary states of the Ottoman Empire">vassal states</a>. Some of these were later absorbed into the empire, while others were granted various types of autonomy during the course of centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> as its capital and control of lands around the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean basin</a>, the Ottoman Empire was at the center of interactions between the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern</a> and Western worlds for six centuries. Following a long period of <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">military setbacks</a> against European powers, the Ottoman Empire gradually <a href="/wiki/Decline_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Decline of the Ottoman Empire">declined</a> in its ability to remain sovereign against competing powers in the late 19th century. 
</p><p>The collapse of the Ottoman Empire was accelerated by the intervention of the great powers. In 1821-1829 the Greeks in their struggle for independence were assisted by the Russian Empire, Great Britain, and the Kingdom of France (see <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a>). 
Later in fact, the Ottoman Empire could exist only in the conditions of acute rivalry of the great powers. Russia's attempt to negotiate with Britain on the partition of the Ottoman Empire failed. Britain after the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Balta_Liman" title="Treaty of Balta Liman">Treaty of Balta Liman</a> in 1838 was interested in preserving the Ottoman Empire and in <a href="/wiki/Crimean_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean war">Crimean war</a> 1853-1856, the great powers of Britain and France opposed Russia, as a result of the Ottoman Empire existed until 1922. As result of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)</a>, Bulgaria, Serbia and Montenegro gained independence in the European part of the Empire.
</p><p>The empire allied with Germany in the early 20th century, with the imperial ambition of recovering its lost territories, but it <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">dissolved</a> in the aftermath of its defeat in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>. At the same time, Turkey itself could barely avoid the fate of being divided into colonies of great powers, see <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a>. The result was the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a>, when Kemalist forces backed by Soviet Russia established the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>. The residue was the new state of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> in the Ottoman Anatolian heartland, as well as the creation of modern <a href="/wiki/Balkan" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan">Balkan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle Eastern</a> states, thus ending Turkish colonial ambitions.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union">Imperial Russia and the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Imperial Russia and the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_communist_party_rule" title="Criticism of communist party rule">Criticism of communist party rule</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Empire" title="Soviet Empire">Soviet Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/220px-Soviet_empire_1960.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/330px-Soviet_empire_1960.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/440px-Soviet_empire_1960.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The maximum territorial extent of countries in the world under Soviet influence, after the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> of 1959 and before the official <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> of 1961</div></div></div>
<p>By the 18th century, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> extended its control to the Pacific, peacefully forming a common border with the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Empire">Qing Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a>. This took place in a large number of military invasions of the lands east, west, and south of it. The <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Russian_War_of_1792" title="Polish–Russian War of 1792">Polish–Russian War of 1792</a> took place after Polish nobility from the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> wrote the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791" title="Constitution of 3 May 1791">Constitution of 3 May 1791</a>. The war resulted in eastern <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> being conquered by Imperial Russia as a colony until 1918. The southern campaigns involved a series of <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">Russo-Persian Wars</a>, which began with the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Expedition_of_1796" title="Persian Expedition of 1796">Persian Expedition of 1796</a>, resulting in the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia (country)</a> as a protectorate. Between 1800 and 1864, Imperial armies invaded south in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_the_Caucasus" title="Russian conquest of the Caucasus">Russian conquest of the Caucasus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Murid_War" title="Murid War">Murid War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Circassian_War" title="Russo-Circassian War">Russo-Circassian War</a>. This last conflict led to the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Circassians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic cleansing of Circassians">ethnic cleansing of Circassians</a> from their lands. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia" title="Russian conquest of Siberia">Russian conquest of Siberia</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Sibir" title="Khanate of Sibir">Khanate of Sibir</a> took place in the 16th and 17th centuries, and resulted in the slaughter of various indigenous tribes by Russians, including the <a href="/wiki/Daur_people" title="Daur people">Daur</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Koryaks" title="Koryaks">Koryaks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Itelmens" title="Itelmens">Itelmens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansi_people" title="Mansi people">Mansi people</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_people" title="Chukchi people">Chukchi</a>. The Russian colonization of Central and Eastern Europe and Siberia and treatment of the resident indigenous peoples has been compared to European colonization of the Americas, with similar negative impacts on the indigenous Siberians as upon the indigenous peoples of the Americas. The extermination of indigenous Siberian tribes was so complete that a relatively small population of only 180,000 are said to exist today. The Russian Empire exploited and suppressed <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a> hosts during this period, before turning them into the special military estate <a href="/wiki/Sosloviye" class="mw-redirect" title="Sosloviye">Sosloviye</a> in the late 18th century. Cossacks were then used in Imperial Russian campaigns against other tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>But it would be a strong simplification to reduce expansion of Russia only to military conquests. The reunification of Ukraine with Russia took place in 1654, when Polish rule brought the population of Ukraine to revolts (see <a href="/wiki/Pereyaslav_Council" title="Pereyaslav Council">Pereyaslav Council</a>). Another example is Georgia's accession to Russia in 1783. Given Georgia's history of invasions from the south, an alliance with Russia may have been seen as the only way to discourage or resist Persian and Ottoman aggression, while also establishing a link to Western Europe (see <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Georgievsk" title="Treaty of Georgievsk">Treaty of Georgievsk</a>). Russia's support helped establish independent Mongolia (independent from China) (see <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Revolution_of_1911" title="Mongolian Revolution of 1911">Mongolian Revolution of 1911</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> leaders had effectively reestablished a polity with roughly the same extent as that empire by 1921, however with an internationalist ideology: Lenin in particular asserted the right to limited self-determination for national minorities within the new territory.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in 1923, the policy of "<a href="/wiki/Indigenization" title="Indigenization">Indigenization</a>" [korenizatsiya] was intended to support non-<a href="/wiki/Russian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian people">Russians</a> develop their national cultures within a socialist framework. Never formally revoked, it stopped being implemented after 1932. After World War II, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> installed socialist regimes modeled on those it had installed in 1919–20 in the old <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, in areas its forces occupied in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The Soviet Union and later the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> supported revolutionary and communist movements in foreign nations and colonies to advance their own interests, but were not always successful.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The USSR provided great assistance to <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> in 1926-1928 in the formation of a unified Chinese government (see <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a>). Although then relations with the USSR deteriorated, but the USSR was the only world power that provided military assistance to China against Japanese aggression in 1937-1941 (see <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Non-Aggression_Pact" title="Sino-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact">Sino-Soviet Non-Aggression Pact</a>). It should be pointed out that the victory of the Chinese Communists in the civil war of 1946-1949 relied on the great help of the USSR (see <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Trotsky</a>, and others, believed that the revolution could only succeed in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a>. Lenin wrote extensively on the matter and famously declared that <a href="/wiki/Imperialism,_the_Highest_Stage_of_Capitalism" title="Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism">Imperialism was the highest stage of</a> <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>. However, after Lenin's death, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> established '<a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_one_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialism in one country">socialism in one country</a>' for the Soviet Union, creating the model for subsequent inward looking Stalinist states and purging the early Internationalist elements. The internationalist tendencies of the early revolution would be abandoned until they returned in the framework of a <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">client state</a> in competition with the Americans during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. In the post-Stalin period in the late 1950s, the new political leader <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> put pressure on the Soviet-American relations starting a new wave of anti-imperialist propaganda. In his speech on the UN conference in 1960, he announced the continuation of the war on imperialism, stating that soon the people of different countries will come together and overthrow their imperialist leaders. Although the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> declared itself <a href="/wiki/Anti-imperialism" title="Anti-imperialism">anti-imperialist</a>, critics argue that it exhibited traits common to historic empires.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-olaf_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olaf-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Some scholars hold that the Soviet Union was a hybrid entity containing elements common to both multinational empires and nation states. Some also argued that the USSR practiced colonialism as did other imperial powers and was carrying on the old Russian tradition of expansion and control.<sup id="cite_ref-olaf_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olaf-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> once argued that the Soviet Union had itself become an <a href="/wiki/Social_imperialism" title="Social imperialism">imperialist power</a> while maintaining a socialist façade. Moreover, the ideas of imperialism were widely spread in action on the higher levels of government. Some Marxists within the Russian Empire and later the USSR, like <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Galiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan Galiev">Sultan Galiev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vasyl_Shakhrai" class="mw-redirect" title="Vasyl Shakhrai">Vasyl Shakhrai</a>, considered the Soviet regime a renewed version of the Russian imperialism and colonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soviet imperialism involved invasion of Hungary in 1956 to destroy democratic forces.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Soviet imperialism was roundly condemned In 1979 when the USSR invaded Afghanistan to keep a friendly government in power. The invasion "alerted the Third World, as no earlier Soviet in intervention a done, to the nature of Soviet imperialism.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> It must be said that the USSR never called itself an "Empire" unlike other world powers and the use of such a name carries a negative connotation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_imperialism" title="American imperialism">American imperialism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_(detailed).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg/220px-Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg/330px-Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg/440px-Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_%28detailed%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1268" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Raising_of_American_flag_at_Iolani_Palace_with_US_Marines_in_the_foreground_(detailed).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ceremonies during the <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Kingdom_of_Hawaii#Annexation" class="mw-redirect" title="Overthrow of the Kingdom of Hawaii">annexation of the Republic of Hawaii</a>, 1898</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG/170px-Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG/255px-Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG/340px-Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2332" data-file-height="3110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Seaport_Museum_226.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cartoon of belligerent <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Sam" title="Uncle Sam">Uncle Sam</a> placing Spain on notice, c. 1898</div></div></div>
<p>Made up of former colonies itself, the early United States expressed its opposition to Imperialism, at least in a form distinct from its own <a href="/wiki/Manifest_Destiny" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifest Destiny">Manifest Destiny</a>, through policies such as the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>. However the US may have unsuccessfully attempted to capture Canada in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. The United States achieved very significant territorial concessions from Mexico during the <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican-American War">Mexican-American War</a>. Beginning in the late 19th and early 20th century, policies such as <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>’s interventionism in Central America and <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>’s mission to "make the world safe for democracy"<sup id="cite_ref-mtholyoke_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtholyoke-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> changed all this. They were often backed by military force, but were more often affected from behind the scenes. This is consistent with the general notion of hegemony and imperium of historical empires.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In 1898, Americans who opposed imperialism created the <a href="/wiki/American_Anti-Imperialist_League" title="American Anti-Imperialist League">Anti-Imperialist League</a> to oppose the <a href="/wiki/US_annexation_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="US annexation of the Philippines">US annexation of the Philippines</a> and Cuba. One year later, a war erupted in the Philippines causing business, labor and government leaders in the US to condemn America's occupation in the Philippines as they also denounced them for causing the deaths of many Filipinos.<sup id="cite_ref-google_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> American foreign policy was denounced as a "racket" by <a href="/wiki/Smedley_Butler" title="Smedley Butler">Smedley Butler</a>, a former American general who had become a spokesman for the far left.<sup id="cite_ref-federalobserver_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-federalobserver-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the start of World War II, President Franklin D. Roosevelt was opposed to European colonialism, especially in India. He pulled back when Britain's Winston Churchill demanded that victory in the war be the first priority. Roosevelt expected that the United Nations would take up the problem of decolonization.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some have described the internal strife between various people groups as a form of imperialism or colonialism. This internal form is distinct from informal U.S. imperialism in the form of political and financial hegemony.<sup id="cite_ref-Empire-_A_Very_Short_Introduction_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-_A_Very_Short_Introduction-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> This internal form of imperialism is also distinct from the United States' formation of "colonies" abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-Empire-_A_Very_Short_Introduction_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-_A_Very_Short_Introduction-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>  Through the treatment of its indigenous peoples during westward expansion, the United States took on the form of an imperial power prior to any attempts at external imperialism. This internal form of empire has been referred to as "internal colonialism".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>  Participation in the African slave trade and the subsequent treatment of its 12 to 15&#160;million Africans is viewed by some to be a more modern extension of America's "internal colonialism".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>  However, this internal colonialism faced resistance, as external colonialism did, but the anti-colonial presence was far less prominent due to the nearly complete dominance that the United States was able to assert over both indigenous peoples and African-Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In his lecture on April 16, 2003, Edward Said made a bold statement on modern imperialism in the United States, whom he described as using aggressive means of attack towards the contemporary Orient, "due to their backward living, lack of democracy and the violation of women’s rights. The western world forgets during this process of converting the other that enlightenment and democracy are concepts that not all will agree upon".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Spanish imperialism in the colonial era corresponds with the rise and decline of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, conventionally recognized as emerging in 1402 with the conquest of the Canary Islands. Following the successes of exploratory maritime voyages conducted during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, such as those undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, Spain committed considerable financial and military resources towards developing a robust navy capable of conducting large-scale, transatlantic expeditionary operations in order to establish and solidify a firm imperial presence across portions of North America, South America, and the geographic regions comprising the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean basin">Caribbean basin</a>. Concomitant with Spanish endorsement and sponsorship of transatlantic expeditionary voyages was the deployment of <i><a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">Conquistadors</a></i>, which further expanded Spanish imperial boundaries through the acquisition and development of territories and colonies.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperialism_in_the_Caribbean_basin">Imperialism in the Caribbean basin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Imperialism in the Caribbean basin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/440px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/660px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/880px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="953" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish colonies and territories in the Caribbean basin (c. 1490 – c. 1660)</div></div></div>
<p>In congruence with the colonialist activities of competing European imperial powers throughout the 15th – 19th centuries, the Spanish were equally engrossed in extending geopolitical power. The Caribbean basin functioned as a key geographic focal point for advancing Spanish imperialism. Similar to the strategic prioritization Spain placed towards achieving victory in the conquests of the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>, Spain placed equal strategic emphasis on expanding the nation's imperial footprint within the Caribbean basin.
</p><p>Echoing the prevailing ideological perspectives regarding colonialism and imperialism embraced by Spain's European rivals during the colonial era, including the English, French, and the Dutch, the Spanish utilized colonialism as a means of expanding imperial geopolitical borders and securing the defense of maritime trade routes in the Caribbean basin.
</p><p>While leveraging colonialism in the same geographic operating theater as its imperial rivals, Spain maintained distinct imperial objectives and instituted a unique form of colonialism in support of its imperial agenda. Spain placed significant strategic emphasis on the acquisition, extraction, and exportation of precious metals (primarily gold and silver). A second objective was the evangelization of subjugated indigenous populations residing in mineral-rich and strategically favorable locations. Notable examples of these indigenous groups include the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taίno</a> populations inhabiting Puerto Rico and segments of Cuba. Compulsory labor and slavery were widely institutionalized across Spanish-occupied territories and colonies, with an initial emphasis on directing labor towards mining activity and related methods of procuring semi-precious metals. The emergence of the <i><a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">Encomienda</a></i> system during the 16th–17th centuries in occupied colonies within the Caribbean basin reflects a gradual shift in imperial prioritization, increasingly focusing on large-scale production and exportation of agricultural commodities.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarly_debate_and_controversy">Scholarly debate and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Imperialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Scholarly debate and controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The scope and scale of Spanish participation in imperialism within the Caribbean basin remains a subject of scholarly debate among historians. A fundamental source of contention stems from the inadvertent conflation of theoretical conceptions of imperialism and colonialism. Furthermore, significant variation exists in the definition and interpretation of these terms as expounded by historians, anthropologists, philosophers, and political scientists.
</p><p>Among historians, there is substantial support in favor of approaching imperialism as a conceptual theory emerging during the 18th–19th centuries, particularly within Britain, propagated by key exponents such as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Chamberlain" title="Joseph Chamberlain">Joseph Chamberlain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a>. In accordance with this theoretical perspective, the activities of the Spanish in the Caribbean are not components of a preeminent, ideologically-driven form of imperialism. Rather, these activities are more accurately classified as representing a form of colonialism.
</p><p>Further divergence among historians can be attributed to varying theoretical perspectives regarding imperialism that are proposed by emerging academic schools of thought. Noteworthy examples include <a href="/wiki/Cultural_imperialism" title="Cultural imperialism">cultural imperialism</a>, whereby proponents such as John Downing and Annabelle Sreberny-Modammadi define imperialism as <i>"...the conquest and control of one country by a more powerful one."</i><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Cultural imperialism signifies the dimensions of the process that go beyond economic exploitation or military force." Moreover, colonialism is understood as <i>"...the form of imperialism in which the government of the colony is run directly by foreigners."</i><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In spite of diverging perspectives and the absence of a unilateral scholarly consensus regarding imperialism among historians, within the context of Spanish expansion in the Caribbean basin during the colonial era, imperialism can be interpreted as an overarching ideological agenda that is perpetuated through the institution of colonialism. In this context, colonialism functions as an instrument designed to achieve specific imperialist objectives.
</p>
